201403	4	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	But if time permits after we have discussed forward guidance, if you have questions for Steve, I’m sure he would be glad to take them up.	92	9
201403	5	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	The main purpose of this meeting is to discuss our forward guidance so that we are able to reach agreement on how to revise it in March.	92	9
201403	6	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	The unemployment rate, at 6.6 percent, is very close to the threshold in our FOMC statement.	92	9
201403	7	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	And despite the weaker tone of recent data, the threshold could be crossed soon, perhaps even before our March meeting.	92	9
201403	8	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	At a minimum, this means that we may need to remove the threshold language at the March meeting.	92	9
201403	9	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	But many of us have expressed an interest in also providing more information about the post-threshold period.	92	9
201403	10	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	In light of the complexities involved in modifying our forward guidance, I thought it would be useful for us to discuss some options outside the context of a regular meeting where the state of the economy and a policy decision take priority.	92	9
201403	11	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	By way of introduction, I would like to make a couple of general comments about forward guidance.	92	9
201403	12	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	I personally see our forward guidance as having served a very important role in keeping financial conditions accommodative and as having thereby supported the recovery.	92	9
201403	13	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	Now that we have finally reached the point when a return to something close to full employment and price stability is in most of our SEP forecasts, issues pertaining to liftoff and normalization will naturally come to play a larger role in our policy communications.	92	9
201403	14	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	I would urge everyone to remain mindful, though, of the numerous “false dawns” the economy has presented.	92	9
201403	15	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	The effective lower bound on interest rates still imposes an important asymmetry on our ability to respond to upside and downside risks.	92	9
201403	16	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	For this reason, and also for purposes of policy continuity, I believe it remains important that our forward guidance continues to convey, in terms that are as clear as possible, the conditions under which policy will remain highly accommodative in order to promote recovery and a lasting end to this lengthy zero- interest-rate episode.	92	9
201403	17	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	We did add some language in December that provided specific information about the Committee’s likely behavior after the 6.5 percent threshold is crossed.	92	9
201403	18	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	And with market expectations now well aligned with both that guidance and our own views, I would personally be quite reluctant to offer less guidance in March than we provided in December and January.	92	9
201403	19	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	There are a number of important issues for us to consider in revising our guidance, and I want to thank the staff for their thoughtful background memo.	92	9
201403	20	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	I appreciate the very useful comments and suggestions that a number of you provided, and they helped shape the memo and the materials circulated for this videoconference.1 For today’s meeting, we have tried to craft a minimal-changes version of our current statement, and it is labeled as option 5.	92	9
201403	21	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	But I asked the staff to focus the memo on changes that go well beyond such a minimal-red-ink approach.	92	9
201403	22	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	Because the crossing of a threshold essentially necessitates a nontrivial revision of the statement, many outside analysts are expecting a change.	92	9
201403	23	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	So the present moment could provide an attractive opportunity for more substantial revisions to the statement.	92	9
201403	24	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	1 The memo “Background Documents and Questions for Discussion on Forward Guidance” used at this meeting by participants is appended to this transcript (appendix 1).	92	9
201403	25	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	With many commentators expecting the forward guidance to change, we will of course have the usual difficulties divining just what observers will make of any changes we decide to adopt or, indeed, what they would make of the absence of much change.	92	9
201403	26	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	Despite these difficulties, I would encourage us to consider whether we could substantially clarify our intentions, remembering, as always, that some minimalist approach, perhaps along the lines of the one circulated by the staff last Friday, will end up being deemed best.	92	9
201403	27	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	Let me highlight four specific issues raised in our prior discussions and in the memo.	92	9
201403	28	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	First, the current guidance is focused on the unemployment rate, but we have consistently communicated that once the threshold is crossed we will be considering a more comprehensive evaluation of the labor market.	92	9
201403	29	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	Now may be an appropriate time to signal this shift in the statement.	92	9
201403	30	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	Some of the options suggested in the staff memo focused on the state of employment relative to our assessment of its maximum sustainable level.	92	9
201403	31	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	This formulation has the virtue of being taken from our Statement of Longer-Run Goals and Monetary Policy Strategy, but this approach would bring a new concept into the statement and might itself seem to call for some new, single measure of slack.	92	9
201403	32	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	Alternatively, the language circulated last Friday simply makes reference to an assessment of whether the recovery in the labor market is complete.	92	9
201403	33	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	This formulation might accurately bring to mind the broad assessment that we actually engage in.	92	9
201403	34	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	Second, over the past several months, the possibility of inflation running persistently and significantly below our objective has become more prominent.	92	9
201403	35	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	It might be appropriate to clarify the role of low inflation in our policy intentions beyond the clause we added in December that specifies that the current target range is likely to be maintained, especially if projected inflation continues to run below the Committee’s 2 percent longer-run goal.	92	9
201403	36	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	The first two options in the staff memo refer explicitly to the shortfall of inflation from our 2 percent objective as a condition determining how long to maintain the current target range for the federal funds rate, and option 3 provides one version of an inflation floor.	92	9
201403	37	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	Third, some of you have indicated in past discussions a preference to clarify the role of financial developments in the statement.	92	9
201403	38	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	This could be warranted, for example, either to address concerns over financial stability, which may grow as the period of highly accommodative policy continues and the economy strengthens, or, alternatively, to convey a willingness of the FOMC to respond if, say, financial conditions tighten in a way that compromises the outlook for attaining our objectives.	92	9
201403	39	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	The options provided by the staff give an approach that encompasses both of these considerations.	92	9
201403	40	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	And option 4 provides an alternative that focuses directly on financial-stability risks.	92	9
201403	41	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	Finally, if the recovery continues as we all hope, we will face an increasing need to clarify how policy will be conducted during the transitional period between liftoff and the time when we settle into some new normal.	92	9
201403	42	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	The current statement mainly suggests that the FOMC will, after liftoff, embrace the balanced approach from the consensus statement.	92	9
201403	43	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	But this is language that sheds little light on policy in the broad range of likely cases in which both employment and inflation are falling short of our objectives, so that any need to balance conflicting objectives remains well in the future.	92	9
201403	44	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	In the new paragraph 6 that is included in the first four options, the staff has provided two sentences pertaining to the post-liftoff period.	92	9
201403	45	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	The first might be viewed as a very general description of the reaction function, whereas the second is focused on the fact that even after we return to price stability and full employment, the appropriate federal funds rate target may remain low relative to what we view as normal in the longer run.	92	9
201403	46	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	Let me stop there with those broad comments that are intended to frame the discussion.	92	9

201403	52	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201403	53	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	Let me be the first, in this group, at least, to welcome you to your new role.	92	9
201403	54	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	I look forward to working with you in your new capacity.	92	9
201403	55	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	I appreciate your framing our discussion as ably as you did.	92	9
201403	56	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	I also found the options and analysis in the memo dated February 21 to be quite valuable, and I want to thank the staff for the great work that was included in that memo.	92	9
201403	57	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	I want to divide my remarks into two parts.	92	9
201403	58	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	First, I’m going to address the question of why we need to provide forward guidance about the future evolution of the federal funds rate.	92	9
201403	59	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	Second, I’ll use the answers to this question to inform my preferred choice among the five options offered to us by the staff.	92	9
201403	60	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	I see two related answers to the question of why we need forward guidance.	92	9
201403	61	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	The first is connected to policy effectiveness.	92	9
201403	62	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	In my view, monetary policy can be effective only if markets and the public have a good understanding of our reaction function.	92	9
201403	63	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	Before the financial crisis, that understanding came from decades of historical experience—historical experience in which the FOMC adhered relatively closely to a well-documented statistical pattern of behavior—that is, something akin to a Taylor rule.	92	9
201403	64	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	In the absence of forward guidance from us, or in the presence of deliberately vague forward guidance like that in option 5, markets are likely to turn back to those pre-crisis historical relationships, like the Taylor (1993) rule or the Taylor (1999) rule, to provide their guide to future FOMC behavior.	92	9
201403	65	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	The problem is that, as the Summary of Economic Projections indicates, monetary policy is likely to be more accommodative than either of these rules for years to come.	92	9
201403	66	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	Given that we are going to deviate from our pre-crisis reaction function, we need to be as informative as we can be about the reaction function that we are actually going to use, and good forward guidance can provide that information.	92	9
201403	67	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	So that’s the effectiveness argument.	92	9
201403	68	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	The second reason why we need to provide forward guidance relates to credibility.	92	9
201403	69	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	Before January 2012, the FOMC did not have an inflation target of 2 percent.	92	9
201403	70	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	Indeed, several FOMC participants, including my predecessor, thought that appropriate policy would be consistent with a long-run average inflation rate noticeably below 2 percent.	92	9
201403	71	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	Against this recent historical backdrop, it would not be at all surprising if the public and markets still saw the new 2 percent inflation marker as being more of a ceiling than a true target.	92	9
201403	72	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	We need to be using our forward guidance about our reaction function to build the credibility of our 2 percent target by assuring the public and markets that we are in fact doing whatever we can to facilitate a rapid return to 2 percent inflation.	92	9
201403	73	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think we need to be using forward guidance to do two things:  to make clear that our reaction function over the next few years will differ importantly from what we did prior to the crisis and, relatedly, to make clear that we are purposefully making choices to keep inflation at 2 percent.	92	9
201403	74	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	Those are the reasons why we use forward guidance.	92	9
201403	75	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	Given those reasons, I see option 3 as being a great example of the kind of guidance that we should think about using.	92	9
201403	76	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	I see option 3 as having four desirable attributes.	92	9
201403	77	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	The first is that it assures the public that the FOMC is highly unlikely to raise the target fed funds rate at least until the one- to two-year-ahead outlook for inflation has risen back to 2 percent.	92	9
201403	78	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	Raising the fed funds rate before that point would imply that we don’t see 2 percent as a true target.	92	9
201403	79	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	Rather, such an action would imply that we continue to see sub–2 percent inflation as being an appropriate outcome for monetary policy.	92	9
201403	80	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	Now, I want to be clear:  The need to wait until the inflation outlook has returned to 2 percent isn’t some arcane result from some fancy-pants theoretical framework.	92	9
201403	81	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	It is an actual description of how inflation-targeting central banks operate in practice.	92	9
201403	82	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	For example, the Bank of Canada has a single mandate—to keep inflation equal to 2 percent.	92	9
201403	83	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	Its operating practice is to adjust policy so that inflation is projected to return to 2 percent over some period of time that is close to 8 quarters, ranging from 6 to 11 quarters.	92	9
201403	84	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	It is true that, unlike the Bank of Canada, we also have an employment mandate, but we want to be clear about what that means for policy.	92	9
201403	85	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	It does not provide a rationalization for raising the federal funds rate before the inflation outlook gets back to 2 percent.	92	9
201403	86	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	The employment mandate is fundamentally asymmetric in nature.	92	9
201403	87	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	It does not say that the FOMC is responsible for making sure that employment doesn’t get too high.	92	9
201403	88	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	It says that the FOMC is responsible for making sure that employment doesn’t stay too low.	92	9
201403	89	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	This asymmetry means that the employment mandate can rationalize being more accommodative than a strict inflation-targeting central bank like the Bank of Canada, but it cannot rationalize being less accommodative than an inflation-targeting central bank.	92	9
201403	90	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	Some observers have suggested that waiting until the outlook for inflation has returned to 2 percent is inconsistent with the FOMC’s historical behavior.	92	9
201403	91	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	That may be right, but historically we didn’t have a 2 percent inflation target.	92	9
201403	92	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	That is a very recent development.	92	9
201403	93	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	It goes back to January 2012.	92	9
201403	94	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	Now that we have a 2 percent inflation target, our actions need to be consistent with that target, not with our past behavior.	92	9
201403	95	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	This is exactly why we need to include this kind of 2 percent inflation floor in our forward guidance.	92	9
201403	96	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	And we need to underscore the message that our future actions will be consistent with that target, not with our past behavior.	92	9
201403	97	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	The second desirable attribute of option 3 is that it does not have an employment threshold.	92	9
201403	98	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think this is going to be challenging for us, because it may seem that, by not including an employment threshold, we are not putting as much emphasis on employment— whereas in fact the opposite is true.	92	9
201403	99	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	An employment threshold actually works against the promotion of maximum employment.	92	9
201403	100	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	The reason is that such a threshold is designed to give the FOMC an escape clause that lets it raise the fed funds rate even though inflation is under control simply because the unemployment rate has gotten too low or employment has gotten too high.	92	9
201403	101	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	For example, even if the inflation outlook is still at 1½ percent, if unemployment falls below, say, 6½ or 6 percent, that kind of threshold gives the FOMC an escape clause that lets it raise rates even though the inflation outlook is still too low.	92	9
201403	102	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	So I see adding such a threshold as being inconsistent with promoting maximum employment, and leaving it out also gets around a lot of problems of trying to define how we want to be thinking about the labor market.	92	9
201403	103	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	A third desirable feature of option 3 is that it appropriately allows for the possibility that the FOMC might choose to alter monetary policy in light of financial market developments either because we want to modulate risks or because we want to loosen financial market conditions.	92	9
201403	104	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think option 3 allows for both of those possibilities.	92	9
201403	105	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	Finally, I like both elements of paragraph 6, both the first and second sentence.	92	9
201403	106	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think the second sentence in particular reminds the public and markets that the FOMC is not returning to its historical patterns of behavior.	92	9
201403	107	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	I’ll close by echoing some of my opening remarks, Madam Chair.	92	9
201403	108	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	We need forward guidance.	92	9
201403	109	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	We need forward guidance to make clear the ways in which our reaction function over the next few years will be different from what we used in the pre-crisis period.	92	9
201403	110	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	And we need forward guidance to make clear to the public that we are fully committed to keeping inflation close to 2 percent.	92	9
201403	111	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think option 3 does a good job on both dimensions.	92	9
201403	112	2014-03-04	confcall	KOCHERLAKOTA	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201403	113	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	Thank you, President Kocherlakota.	92	9
201403	114	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	President Bullard.	92	9
201403	115	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	Thank you, Madam Chair, and welcome to your new role.	92	9
201403	116	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	I’m looking forward to it, and I see that today we have lined up a mind-numbingly complex discussion for you to navigate, so I think that’s a good way for you to get started in your new role.	92	9
201403	117	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	As I suspect many of you did, I appreciated the staff memos on this topic.	92	9
201403	118	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	They really helped my thinking, and so did the comments on the staff memos from several presidents.	92	9
201403	119	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	I will organize my discussion here around three issues that are key from my perspective, which actually dovetail with what you said, Madam Chair, in your opening remarks.	92	9
201403	120	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	The first question is:  Does the Committee wish to take this opportunity to change out the real variable in the qualitative description of our reaction function from unemployment to employment or, possibly, to some other real variable?	92	9
201403	121	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	The second question is:  Is there a case to be made for making inflation the focus variable and deemphasizing any real variable?	92	9
201403	122	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	And the third question is;  How should the Committee reference financial-stability issues?	92	9
201403	123	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	I’m going to talk mainly about these three issues here and not too much about the fourth issue that you mentioned, Madam Chair.	92	9
201403	124	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	I will comment on each of these questions in turn and, along the way, on some of the specific alternatives that were put forward in the memos.	92	9
201403	125	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	Let me just foreshadow my conclusion here.	92	9
201403	126	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	My comments are modestly negative on the options in front of the Committee.	92	9
201403	127	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	My bottom line is that, as a practical matter, the Committee should proceed with changes to the existing thresholds in a minimalist way, relying mostly on simple qualitative language.	92	9
201403	128	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	Attempts to do more in the current circumstances may cause more problems for the Committee than they solve.	92	9
201403	129	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	So let me reach that conclusion by discussing these three questions.	92	9
201403	130	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	Question 1 was, should the Committee take this opportunity to change out the key real variable in the existing qualitative description of our reaction function from unemployment to employment or, possibly, to some other real variable?	92	9
201403	131	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	Several of the alternatives suggest that the Committee no longer refer to unemployment and instead use “the projected shortfall of employment from its maximum sustainable level.”	92	9
201403	132	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	I have several comments on this particular language.	92	9
201403	133	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	First, I think we should keep in mind that it may be a minor shock to financial markets, households, and businesses that we are no longer referring explicitly to unemployment.	92	9
201403	134	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	I am not sure how markets will actually react to this.	92	9
201403	135	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	Many understand that we are unlikely to retain an explicit numerical threshold for unemployment as the economy nears more normal performance, but removing the reference completely may come as something of a surprise.	92	9
201403	136	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	Second, and perhaps more important, I think that considerable uncertainty may attend the very notion of an employment shortfall, as well as how the Committee intends to measure it.	92	9
201403	137	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	I think it would be very hard for financial markets to infer, based on what we have so far provided, what this phrase means for the date of liftoff.	92	9
201403	138	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	One reason for this is that employment projections are not in the SEP, so it seems like we would have to provide information outside the SEP process as to what might be considered an appropriate employment level.	92	9
201403	139	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	On balance, my judgment is that changing the reference from “unemployment” to “employment” in this way may create unwanted uncertainty around future FOMC intentions.	92	9
201403	140	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	This can, of course, be managed, but I think it may be quite difficult.	92	9
201403	141	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	This thought leads to the idea that the Committee might wish to use an alternative real variable.	92	9
201403	142	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	In a comment to the Committee, I suggested real output growth as that alternative variable.	92	9
201403	143	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	This has several advantages.	92	9
201403	144	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	First, unlike employment levels, which are not projected in the SEP, output growth is explicitly in the current SEP.	92	9
201403	145	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	This would give financial market participants and others in the economy a clear indication of what the Committee is expecting with respect to the key real variable mentioned in the statement.	92	9
201403	146	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	Second, in my view, a move toward more emphasis on output growth would move the Committee closer to traditional approaches to monetary policy as the economy continues to normalize.	92	9
201403	147	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	Referencing output growth also has the advantage, according to some studies, of avoiding monetary policy mistakes associated with level-based output or employment gaps.	92	9
201403	148	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	Athanasios Orphanides, in particular, is one author who has emphasized the pitfalls of gap mismeasurement and has suggested that output growth rates might provide better guidance for monetary policymakers.	92	9
201403	149	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	Some of you may worry that output growth today is relatively robust and, therefore, that this might suggest a more aggressive policy than the Committee intends.	92	9
201403	150	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	But, in my view, even with a reference in the statement to output growth as the key real variable, accommodative policy can still be rationalized because of today’s lower-than-expected inflation outcomes.	92	9
201403	151	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	I recognize, Madam Chair, that the Committee may not be willing to go in this direction at this time, but I think that if we want to change out unemployment for a new real variable, this might be a reasonable alternative—if not now, then perhaps at some point in the future.	92	9
201403	152	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	As you suggested, Madam Chair, this meeting is probably a good opportunity to at least consider possible alternatives, and that’s why I’m putting this one forward.	92	9
201403	153	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	This leads to my second question—namely, is there a case to be made for making inflation the focus variable and deemphasizing references to a real variable?	92	9
201403	154	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	This idea is contained in option 3 in the staff memo.	92	9
201403	155	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	I think there is a compelling case for going in this direction, which I would characterize as something closer to strict inflation targeting.	92	9
201403	156	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	This type of option would make clear that the Committee prefers real variables to be as robust as possible, provided that no serious inflation problem develops, and so does not require the Committee to put explicit limits on either levels or growth rates of real variables.	92	9
201403	157	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	Here I am unwittingly echoing some of the arguments that President Kocherlakota just made, particularly the idea that perhaps the Committee would not want to be putting such limits on real variables.	92	9
201403	158	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	After all, we want low unemployment, high employment, and so on.	92	9
201403	159	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	Surely this approach has much to commend it in terms of transparency, simplicity, and—	92	9
201403	160	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	I believe—consistency with what the Committee truly desires.	92	9
201403	161	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	Why should the Committee put limits on what it thinks may be realistic in terms of levels of unemployment, employment, or output growth when those limits are only educated guesses in any event?	92	9
201403	162	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	Would it not be better to react directly to evidence on inflation alone and simply set monetary policy accordingly?	92	9
201403	163	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	If this means that unemployment can move to very low levels, employment levels can be quite high, and output growth rates can soar, is this not all the better?	92	9
201403	164	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	The answer is that, indeed, it would be better, and so, in many ways, I think that promoting inflation as the key variable in our communication has much to recommend it.	92	9
201403	165	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	Still, my sense is that the Committee may not be ready to go in the strict inflation- targeting direction, and, in any event, I think option 3 as written does have one important problem.	92	9
201403	166	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	The problem, at least in my view, is that the text refers to projected inflation between one and two years ahead.	92	9
201403	167	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	I do not think it is credible for a central bank to project inflation over the medium term as being different from target, at least under ordinary circumstances.	92	9
201403	168	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	Indeed, as President Kocherlakota just stressed, the very criterion for optimal inflation-targeting policy in many models would be to set policy exactly so that inflation would be projected to equal the target over the medium term.	92	9
201403	169	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	Any projection that does not meet this criterion would normally be viewed as involving suboptimal policy, because the central bank could increase the amount of accommodation in a way that would make the projection equal to target over the medium term.	92	9
201403	170	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	Because of this difficulty, I see the adoption of the approach in option 3 as problematic from a communications perspective.	92	9
201403	171	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	If the Committee’s inflation forecast does not equal the target over the medium term, why doesn’t the Committee simply increase the amount of accommodation so that the inflation forecast does equal the target over the medium term?	92	9
201403	172	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	This brings me to question 3, which is how to handle references to financial stability in the statement.	92	9
201403	173	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	On this topic, I think a minimalist reference is appropriate.	92	9
201403	174	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	We need to show that the topic is understood by the Committee without overstating how much of a factor this may be in Committee decisionmaking.	92	9
201403	175	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	The “irrational exuberance” speech by former Chairman Greenspan was given in 1996, and since that time, the Committee has struggled with two extraordinary bubbles in the US economy.	92	9
201403	176	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	The debate on monetary policy and bubbles continues to rage.	92	9
201403	177	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	I do not think that anyone inside or outside the Fed has to be reminded that financial stability is an important concern in the making of monetary policy.	92	9
201403	178	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	If we make a minimal reference to financial stability, that will be sufficient to remind everyone that we are fully cognizant of this issue.	92	9
201403	179	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	The considerations I have emphasized suggest that option 5, with its more minimalist approach to changing the language in the Committee’s forward guidance paragraph, is most likely to succeed in delivering the continuity sought by the Committee in contemplating this change of language.	92	9
201403	180	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	This approach simply removes the thresholds and replaces the previous text with references to a wide variety of indicators and a notion of complete recovery in labor markets in the future.	92	9
201403	181	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	This last criterion will cause some uncertainty as to its meaning but at the same time suggest that a judgment call will have to be made by the Committee based on a wide variety of factors.	92	9
201403	182	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	This is a better approach for the time being and, in my view, moves the Committee somewhat closer to normal monetary policy.	92	9
201403	183	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	An oblique reference to financial stability is included through the phrase “readings on financial developments.”	92	9
201403	184	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	On balance, then, Madam Chair, I prefer option 5 of the options presented to the Committee for its use of mostly qualitative language to replace our existing thresholds on unemployment and inflation.	92	9
201403	185	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	The other options suffer from key drawbacks that I think would introduce unwanted uncertainty into financial markets’ understanding of Committee intentions.	92	9
201403	186	2014-03-04	confcall	BULLARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9

201403	189	2014-03-04	confcall	ROSENGREN	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9

201403	191	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	Thank you.	92	9
201403	192	2014-03-04	confcall	ROSENGREN	My hope is that the forward guidance language we choose does the following.	92	9
201403	193	2014-03-04	confcall	ROSENGREN	First, as in the memo on the different options for forward guidance, I believe the language should have a neutral effect on expectations.	92	9
201403	194	2014-03-04	confcall	ROSENGREN	Expectations seem appropriately aligned with the Committee’s thinking at this time.	92	9
201403	195	2014-03-04	confcall	ROSENGREN	Given the weakness in incoming data, I would certainly not want the language to tighten financial conditions.	92	9
201403	196	2014-03-04	confcall	ROSENGREN	Second, given the market focus on calendar dates, the language needs to avoid adding to uncertainty around the implications for our current thinking on the likely liftoff date.	92	9
201403	197	2014-03-04	confcall	ROSENGREN	This is achieved by the statement that the current target range for the federal funds rate will be maintained “for a considerable time after the asset purchase program ends.”	92	9
201403	198	2014-03-04	confcall	ROSENGREN	It is tied to our actions—namely, the tapering program.	92	9
201403	199	2014-03-04	confcall	ROSENGREN	Since the tapering program can be slowed down or sped up, it has flexibility.	92	9
201403	200	2014-03-04	confcall	ROSENGREN	However, the modal interpretation of this language will be that liftoff would likely occur in the latter half of 2015.	92	9
201403	201	2014-03-04	confcall	ROSENGREN	Third, the language should be as simple as possible.	92	9
201403	202	2014-03-04	confcall	ROSENGREN	The difference between purchases and liftoff and between triggers and thresholds has been surprisingly difficult to communicate, as witnessed both by the rise in short-term rates that followed the announcement of possible tapering in the middle of last year and by the confusion that persists around the 6½ percent threshold.	92	9
201403	203	2014-03-04	confcall	ROSENGREN	In my view, the option that gets closest to these objectives is option 2.	92	9
201403	204	2014-03-04	confcall	ROSENGREN	It is designed to have a neutral effect on expectations, provides clarity on likely liftoff, and has a relatively simple construction.	92	9
201403	205	2014-03-04	confcall	ROSENGREN	However, I think it should be simplified further.	92	9
201403	206	2014-03-04	confcall	ROSENGREN	For option 2, paragraph 5, I would substitute the first area highlighted in blue with “the Committee will consider the projected pace at which labor markets are normalizing and the projected pace at which inflation returns to the Committee’s longer-run goal of 2 percent.	92	9
201403	207	2014-03-04	confcall	ROSENGREN	In assessing the improvement in labor market conditions, the Committee will consider a broad range of indicators.”	92	9
201403	208	2014-03-04	confcall	ROSENGREN	The concept of normalizing seems more consistent with the concept of the long-run unemployment forecast provided in the SEP, although normalizing would incorporate more than just the unemployment rate.	92	9
201403	209	2014-03-04	confcall	ROSENGREN	For option 2, paragraph 5, I would substitute the second area highlighted in blue with “at least as long as labor market conditions are in the process of normalizing, inflation projected between one and two years ahead does not significantly exceed 2 percent, and longer-term inflation expectations continue to be well anchored.”	92	9
201403	210	2014-03-04	confcall	ROSENGREN	This refers back to returning to normalized labor markets.	92	9
201403	211	2014-03-04	confcall	ROSENGREN	It also replaces language that sounds like an inflation ceiling, “does not exceed 2 percent,” with “does not significantly exceed 2 percent.”	92	9
201403	212	2014-03-04	confcall	ROSENGREN	In terms of the other questions, I would not include language on financial developments at this time.	92	9
201403	213	2014-03-04	confcall	ROSENGREN	I do not believe we have clarity or consensus on this issue yet, and we probably need to have much more discussion on that topic.	92	9
201403	214	2014-03-04	confcall	ROSENGREN	I am comfortable with paragraph 6 in options 1 through 3, and I would highlight one concern, which is that some of the SEP submissions may not be consistent with the guidance we are providing.	92	9
201403	215	2014-03-04	confcall	ROSENGREN	This is likely to provide less clarity than desirable, and it highlights more work that needs to be done on the SEP.	92	9
201403	216	2014-03-04	confcall	ROSENGREN	Ideally, how we report the SEP should be as consistent as possible with any guidance provided in the statement.	92	9

201403	220	2014-03-04	confcall	LOCKHART	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201403	221	2014-03-04	confcall	LOCKHART	I would like to comment on broad communications tactics as regards forward guidance as well as the substance of the statement.	92	9
201403	222	2014-03-04	confcall	LOCKHART	I will respond to some of the questions as I proceed.	92	9
201403	223	2014-03-04	confcall	LOCKHART	First, I would caution against going too far in reliance on the statement alone as our tool to transmit guidance.	92	9
201403	224	2014-03-04	confcall	LOCKHART	A point I’ve made before in Committee meetings is that the Committee is designed to arrive at a common decision, not necessarily a uniformly held rationale for decisions.	92	9
201403	225	2014-03-04	confcall	LOCKHART	So I prefer an approach to crafting the statement that treats it as a vehicle for communicating a framework, or a general statement, for our determination of the path of policy.	92	9
201403	226	2014-03-04	confcall	LOCKHART	I see the statement as a device for implementing forward guidance as having a tactical role within a set of communications alternatives, each with its own array of possible tactical uses.	92	9
201403	227	2014-03-04	confcall	LOCKHART	These other communications devices are the Chair’s press conference, the SEPs, the minutes, the Chair’s speeches and testimony, our collective speaking opportunities, and, maybe, other devices to be developed.	92	9
201403	228	2014-03-04	confcall	LOCKHART	The use of these alternative communications vehicles can convey more information, appropriately qualified details, and general color or can draw attention to quantification in the SEP of elements of the statement.	92	9
201403	229	2014-03-04	confcall	LOCKHART	Proper governance, however, is a legitimate concern.	92	9
201403	230	2014-03-04	confcall	LOCKHART	The principle of Committee ratification of the content of formal communications requires, it seems to me, a disciplined process around use of some of the alternative communications devices.	92	9
201403	231	2014-03-04	confcall	LOCKHART	As we move ahead to refine our communications strategy, I’d like to see us wrestle in good time with how to do all of this and deal with communications as a package.	92	9
201403	232	2014-03-04	confcall	LOCKHART	I can envision a checklist of sorts for composing and updating a statement to convey a framework for policy decisions.	92	9
201403	233	2014-03-04	confcall	LOCKHART	It might include elements such as an assessment of progress toward qualitative goals, a projection of progress over a time horizon, a reference to a broad set of indicators, and critical considerations in setting or changing policies.	92	9
201403	234	2014-03-04	confcall	LOCKHART	Of the five options presented, option 5 comes closest to what I have in mind.	92	9
201403	235	2014-03-04	confcall	LOCKHART	I think it adequately covers the financial developments consideration, and if we view financial stability as a distinct consideration, I would not be averse to language like that in option 4 on financial stability per se.	92	9
201403	236	2014-03-04	confcall	LOCKHART	A statement that serves to communicate a framework would almost of necessity rely on qualitative measures of economic conditionality.	92	9
201403	237	2014-03-04	confcall	LOCKHART	Reliance in the statement on qualitative measures allows, in my mind, for interpretation elsewhere, particularly in press conferences.	92	9
201403	238	2014-03-04	confcall	LOCKHART	I would, therefore, drop the use of thresholds, targets, or triggers.	92	9
201403	239	2014-03-04	confcall	LOCKHART	I do not favor linking the timing of the first increase of the federal funds rate to the asset purchase program.	92	9
201403	240	2014-03-04	confcall	LOCKHART	I view the wind- down as likely to continue on the current track unless the economy deteriorates markedly.	92	9
201403	241	2014-03-04	confcall	LOCKHART	This makes the terminal point of asset purchases fairly predictable.	92	9
201403	242	2014-03-04	confcall	LOCKHART	Linking liftoff to the end of the asset purchase program introduces a date feature that I believe the Committee is trying to avoid.	92	9
201403	243	2014-03-04	confcall	LOCKHART	I also do not favor introducing an inflation floor, at least not at this time.	92	9
201403	244	2014-03-04	confcall	LOCKHART	And I do not think it’s necessary yet to introduce additional guidance on the path of the policy rate post-liftoff.	92	9
201403	245	2014-03-04	confcall	LOCKHART	The conditions for liftoff are still down the road, and I would prefer to assess and communicate our exit strategy with a clearer view of what conditions are likely to be at that time.	92	9
201403	246	2014-03-04	confcall	LOCKHART	I see potential for misinterpretation of how near the liftoff date might be, so I would hold fire on additional post-liftoff guidance at this time.	92	9
201403	247	2014-03-04	confcall	LOCKHART	However, I do not particularly object to the existing post-liftoff language.	92	9
201403	248	2014-03-04	confcall	LOCKHART	Those are my comments.	92	9

201403	258	2014-03-04	confcall	FISHER	In considering all of this, I am very mindful of the fact that, first, we really don’t know— at least, I don’t believe we can successfully articulate with precision—what a maximum sustainable level of employment or of output growth relative to long-term trend actually is.	92	9

201403	265	2014-03-04	confcall	FISHER	To begin, I believe that it would be ideal for the Committee to decide on a strategy for conducting post-liftoff monetary policy and also on a plan for communicating that strategy to the public—through statements but also through our speeches, and particularly through your press conferences—either before or in conjunction with the new forward guidance on liftoff.	92	9
201403	266	2014-03-04	confcall	FISHER	I think this is a sensible way to proceed for two reasons.	92	9

201403	298	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	President Williams.	92	9
201403	299	2014-03-04	confcall	WILLIAMS	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201403	300	2014-03-04	confcall	WILLIAMS	I actually find myself in complete agreement with the comments of President Rosengren.	92	9
201403	301	2014-03-04	confcall	WILLIAMS	Nevertheless, I will make my own comments, and I have my own version of paragraph 5, which is similar in spirit to President Rosengren’s comments but, I think, is something that may be even a little simpler.	92	9
201403	302	2014-03-04	confcall	WILLIAMS	As we move from the extraordinary times of the past several years to more ordinary times, our policy statements and forward guidance should move away from numeric thresholds, triggers, and floors, as many people have already mentioned.	92	9
201403	303	2014-03-04	confcall	WILLIAMS	Instead, the statement should provide a more qualitative explanation of our policy reaction function in the context of the economic situation and our goals.	92	9
201403	304	2014-03-04	confcall	WILLIAMS	Over time, the statement should become shorter and should not try to cover all possible issues and contingencies.	92	9
201403	305	2014-03-04	confcall	WILLIAMS	In considering the qualitative versus quantitative guidance, I think of the analogy of giving someone instructions on how to get to Disneyland from Northern California—say, from Sacramento.	92	9
201403	306	2014-03-04	confcall	WILLIAMS	And the first part of it is, get on I−5, go south for several hours, and just keep going.	92	9
201403	307	2014-03-04	confcall	WILLIAMS	That’s what I see as our threshold language of a 6½ percent unemployment rate, and I think that served us very well.	92	9
201403	308	2014-03-04	confcall	WILLIAMS	Eventually, you start going over the Grapevine, you come into Los Angeles, and you run into the massive traffic there, road closures, and situations that you did not expect.	92	9
201403	309	2014-03-04	confcall	WILLIAMS	Obviously, there you have to use judgment, and you have to adapt to a change in circumstances.	92	9
201403	310	2014-03-04	confcall	WILLIAMS	So any attempt to explain to somebody how you navigate through an area like Los Angeles in a predetermined way is going to fail.	92	9
201403	311	2014-03-04	confcall	WILLIAMS	I think that, as we’ve gotten closer to our goals, we are facing a choice to either say, “Well, keep going on I−5 at full speed”—the danger with that is, you end up in Mexico—or try to explain all of the contingencies and the factors and the thresholds that you should be following.	92	9
201403	312	2014-03-04	confcall	WILLIAMS	And it’s better to try to provide more of the framework, the reaction function, and not try to explain all of the conditions and contingencies.	92	9
201403	313	2014-03-04	confcall	WILLIAMS	I see three primary goals of the March FOMC statement:  first, to reaffirm the public’s understanding of our policy approach and our plans—that is, keep policy expectations basically where they are today; second, to provide a bridge between the end of our asset purchase program and the date of funds rate liftoff; and, third, to provide a general contour of how we expect to see policy in the post-liftoff period.	92	9
201403	314	2014-03-04	confcall	WILLIAMS	Many of the proposals in the staff memo, in my view, try to do too much, distracting attention from these three basic goals.	92	9
201403	315	2014-03-04	confcall	WILLIAMS	I think we can be clearer and more effective if we keep the statement language more similar to that of January but, at the same time, importantly, anchor interest rate expectations appropriately.	92	9
201403	316	2014-03-04	confcall	WILLIAMS	Toward this end, I have my own four-sentence version of paragraph 5, which I will read, and it goes like this:  “To support continued progress toward maximum employment and price stability, the Committee today reaffirmed its view that a highly accommodative stance of monetary policy will remain appropriate for a considerable time after the asset purchase program ends.	92	9
201403	317	2014-03-04	confcall	WILLIAMS	In determining how long to maintain the current range of 0 to ¼ percent for the fed funds rate, the Committee will consider actual and expected future progress of unemployment and inflation toward their mandate-consistent levels.	92	9
201403	318	2014-03-04	confcall	WILLIAMS	This assessment will take into account a wide range of information, including various measures of labor market conditions, indicators of inflation pressures and inflation expectations, and readings on financial developments.	92	9
201403	319	2014-03-04	confcall	WILLIAMS	The Committee currently anticipates it will be appropriate to maintain the current range for the federal funds rate until significant further progress toward its goals is achieved, provided that longer-term inflation expectations continue to be well anchored and risks to financial stability remain contained.”	92	9
201403	320	2014-03-04	confcall	WILLIAMS	I am also comfortable with including paragraph 6.	92	9
201403	321	2014-03-04	confcall	WILLIAMS	This approach anchors interest rate expectations in three ways.	92	9
201403	322	2014-03-04	confcall	WILLIAMS	First, it retains and highlights the “considerable time after the asset purchase program ends” phrasing, which I think is important.	92	9
201403	323	2014-03-04	confcall	WILLIAMS	Second, it states that we will maintain the funds rate at its current level until significant further progress toward our goals is achieved, and, of course, it makes reference to both of our goals.	92	9
201403	324	2014-03-04	confcall	WILLIAMS	And, third, the inclusion of paragraph 6 should help anchor expectations about the path after liftoff.	92	9
201403	325	2014-03-04	confcall	WILLIAMS	Now, regarding the questions in the staff memo, paragraphs 2 to 4 of the FOMC statement already discuss the general principles of our approach to policy, so we don’t really need to restate the general approach in paragraph 5, in my view.	92	9
201403	326	2014-03-04	confcall	WILLIAMS	I would also mention at that point that it’s important in thinking about paragraph 5 to reread paragraphs 2 through 4.	92	9
201403	327	2014-03-04	confcall	WILLIAMS	There is a lot of discussion there about objectives or appropriate stance of policy, and, in thinking about paragraph 5, you want to realize that that whole set-up is around asset purchases.	92	9
201403	328	2014-03-04	confcall	WILLIAMS	So, in my view, you want to start paragraph 5 with a reference to the end of asset purchases.	92	9
201403	329	2014-03-04	confcall	WILLIAMS	With respect to financial developments, I think the current discussion in the FOMC statement, the very brief mention of it, is appropriate and encompasses consideration of financial-stability issues.	92	9
201403	330	2014-03-04	confcall	WILLIAMS	And, to repeat a comment that has already been made, we want to be careful to avoid the appearance that we have a particular target for asset prices in mind.	92	9
201403	331	2014-03-04	confcall	WILLIAMS	Finally, to even better anchor policy expectations during this transition period, we could start publishing the median of the SEP forecasts for the current set of voters on the Committee in addition to what we currently publish.	92	9
201403	332	2014-03-04	confcall	WILLIAMS	In my view, this approach would preserve the strengths of presenting the full set of SEP submissions, which gives you the full range of views of all of the 19 participants but, importantly, would give a clearer view of the center of the Committee, which would provide hard numbers to reinforce the message in the statement.	92	9

201403	336	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201403	337	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	The economic and global environments continue to call for strongly accommodative monetary policy in the United States.	92	9
201403	338	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	In this context, it has been extremely important that the public and financial markets understand that the funds rate would remain at zero for a long time.	92	9
201403	339	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	Our threshold forward guidance has worked well to solidify the public’s understanding on this dimension, and the economic conditionality of our guidance has been pretty well understood.	92	9
201403	340	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	Frankly, this has been quite successful to date.	92	9
201403	341	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	Furthermore, as noted by the staff, market expectations currently appear well aligned with the FOMC views on how policy is likely to evolve, and I agree with the principle that we don’t want our new statement to alter that view.	92	9
201403	342	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	So I am in favor of maintaining a form of forward guidance in the statement.	92	9
201403	343	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	It simply is key for maintaining the necessary high degree of monetary accommodation as we go forward.	92	9
201403	344	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	Any changes to the forward guidance in our FOMC statement should be consistent with a number of uncontroversial key elements.	92	9
201403	345	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	First, our guidance should clearly demonstrate fidelity to our January 2012 Longer-Run Goals and Monetary Policy Strategy.	92	9
201403	346	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	We should be expressing our clear intention to meet our dual-mandate goals in a timely and balanced fashion.	92	9
201403	347	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	And we should repeatedly ask if our policy formulation is consistent with this important formulation.	92	9
201403	348	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	This takes me to the second element.	92	9
201403	349	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	We should mention both sides of our dual mandate prominently in the guidance—both the real side and inflation.	92	9
201403	350	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	Third, central bankers, in general, have difficulty acknowledging that an inflation objective should be evaluated symmetrically around its long-run goal.	92	9
201403	351	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	I agree with the comments of President Kocherlakota on this.	92	9
201403	352	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	Our policy commentary should be construed with sufficient care to be convincing to the public that 2 percent is not a ceiling for inflation.	92	9
201403	353	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	Fourth, the overall stance of monetary policy is characterized by both the current settings and the entire expected path for our policy tools.	92	9
201403	354	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	This means that our guidance should include commentary that adequately captures our future policy intentions for the funds rate after its initial liftoff from zero.	92	9
201403	355	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	With these elements in mind, and considering the history of the Committee’s discussions on the subject of forward guidance, I’m most drawn to option 5, which contains the smallest changes to the January forward guidance.	92	9
201403	356	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	I find its conditional guidance for not lifting rates, as long as projected inflation is under 2 percent, to be workable and acceptable.	92	9
201403	357	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	With regard to the employment side of the mandate, I personally like using highly explicit conditional criteria in our forward guidance.	92	9
201403	358	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	However, I know that reducing the unemployment threshold is off the table.	92	9
201403	359	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	I also recognize that the somewhat unusual behavior of the unemployment rate of late suggests that it might not be the best marker to use today.	92	9
201403	360	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	Circumstances certainly are different than when we brought it into the statement in the fall of 2012.	92	9
201403	361	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	The other options seem to have more challenges, in my opinion.	92	9
201403	362	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	In the abstract, I am drawn to the threshold for the level of employment in option 2 that is associated with maximum employment.	92	9
201403	363	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	However, I don’t have a lot of confidence that we’re going to be able to operationalize it well.	92	9
201403	364	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	If anyone has more imagination than I do on how to operationalize this, then I’d be interested in marrying it with the explicit inflation objective threshold in option 3.	92	9
201403	365	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	But, in my opinion, option 3 alone lacks sufficient real-side conditionality.	92	9
201403	366	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	That’s still important.	92	9
201403	367	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	I doubt that inflation is going to increase very quickly, and I don’t think it’s going to increase to 2 percent very soon.	92	9
201403	368	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	But if it did and the unemployment rate was at 6½ percent, or just a little bit above, I think a balanced approach calls for patience in adjusting our funds rate, and having both of them in the forward guidance is helpful in that regard.	92	9
201403	369	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	So I tend to prefer option 5.	92	9
201403	370	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	With some very small modifications, I think it could be reasonably workable.	92	9
201403	371	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	The most important attribute in this formulation, for me, is the description of the labor market guideline—that is, “at least as long as complete recovery in the labor market appears to be more than a year away.”	92	9
201403	372	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	This is clever and is broadly consistent with many ways one might want to formulate a labor market threshold.	92	9
201403	373	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	For example, if the unemployment rate fell to 6 percent, or even a little bit below that, I might expect that 5½ percent unemployment is in reach within a year—maybe.	92	9
201403	374	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	It gets closer to my policy intention, as I would expect it to be formulated in line with the January 2012 longer-run goals statement.	92	9
201403	375	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	It also allows for a wide array of labor market data to be included in the conditionality test—employment levels, employment-to-population ratios and labor force participation rates relative to trends, and hiring and quits developments.	92	9
201403	376	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	And the statement could be modified to mention, a little bit more than it does currently, that we will consider a broad array of such indicators.	92	9
201403	377	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	Some other improvement opportunities are the following:  The option should add the horizon for the inflation projections to be one to two years ahead, as in the other options.	92	9
201403	378	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	And President Rosengren had a suggestion that this language could be adjusted a little bit to mention that, as long as inflation didn’t “significantly exceed 2 percent”—I think that would be helpful.	92	9
201403	379	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	That would also demonstrate that our 2 percent longer-run inflation objective is not a ceiling.	92	9
201403	380	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	And the option should append mention of our taking account of financial developments and their implications for attaining the Committee’s dual-mandate objectives, as in the last sentence of option 3, paragraph 5.	92	9
201403	381	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	Lastly, a description of the post-liftoff path for short-term interest rates could be enhanced in one of the various paragraph 6 options, as in paragraph 6 of option 3—that fits nicely.	92	9
201403	382	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	Our  SEP forecasts for 2016 have us at our mandate goals, and the funds rate is about 2 percent.	92	9
201403	383	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	That’s going to be challenging for the public and financial market participants.	92	9
201403	384	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	I think when you go out and talk to people, anybody who is knowledgeable and is aware of that will ask what we mean by that.	92	9
201403	385	2014-03-04	confcall	EVANS	This paragraph helps address that, and I would support its inclusion.	92	9

201403	388	2014-03-04	confcall	YELLEN	Vice President Weinberg, who is substituting for President Lacker.	92	9
201403	389	2014-03-04	confcall	WEINBERG	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201403	390	2014-03-04	confcall	WEINBERG	It’s clearly an opportune and appropriate time to modify forward guidance, given the approaching 6½ percent unemployment threshold.	92	9
201403	391	2014-03-04	confcall	WEINBERG	At the moment, there doesn’t seem to be much of a case for trying to significantly shift market expectations for the path of short-term interest rates, as market expectations appear to be pretty well aligned with the Committee’s center of gravity as displayed in the SEP, for example.	92	9
201403	392	2014-03-04	confcall	WEINBERG	One of the key questions in thinking about what to communicate is how to describe conditions that would lead to an initial interest rate increase.	92	9
201403	393	2014-03-04	confcall	WEINBERG	The Committee has really not spent much time discussing the economic conditions that, for each participant, would likely trigger wanting to raise rates for the first time.	92	9
201403	394	2014-03-04	confcall	WEINBERG	On this, there is probably a wide range of views around the table.	92	9
201403	395	2014-03-04	confcall	WEINBERG	Accordingly, anything more than a fairly minimalist approach could be premature at this point.	92	9
201403	396	2014-03-04	confcall	WEINBERG	Trying to articulate something more precise involves implicitly staking out the conceptual framework, and more discussions about the framework might be useful before doing so.	92	9
201403	397	2014-03-04	confcall	WEINBERG	Our preference would be for a streamlined version of option 5 in which the third and fourth sentences are combined to read as follows: “The Committee anticipates, based on its assessment of these factors, that it likely will be appropriate to maintain the current 0 to ¼ percent target range for the federal funds rate for a considerable time after the asset purchase program ends.”	92	9
201403	398	2014-03-04	confcall	WEINBERG	This eliminates the clause “at least as long as complete recovery in the labor market appears to be more than a year away, especially if projected inflation continues to run below the Committee’s 2 percent longer-run goal.”	92	9
201403	399	2014-03-04	confcall	WEINBERG	You could call this a “hyper-minimalist approach.”	92	9
201403	400	2014-03-04	confcall	WEINBERG	While the “complete recovery” language in option 5 is intentionally less specific, and that is appealing in some regards, I think that people seeing that language are naturally going to want to map it to a specific unemployment rate or an employment-to-population ratio or some other metric.	92	9
201403	401	2014-03-04	confcall	WEINBERG	Using a phrase like “complete recovery” or “maximum sustainable level of employment” in this context seems to go beyond the Committee’s consensus statement of 2012, which states that “the maximum level of employment is largely determined by nonmonetary factors” and which emphasizes its variability.	92	9
201403	402	2014-03-04	confcall	WEINBERG	Granted, the consensus statement goes on to cite participants’ estimates of the longer-run normal rate of unemployment, but it never actually equates that concept with the maximum level of employment.	92	9
201403	403	2014-03-04	confcall	WEINBERG	In the current context, pivoting from an unemployment rate threshold to a formulation that refers to “maximum sustainable level of employment” risks looking opportunistic, as if the Committee is responding to the fall in the unemployment rate by shifting to other labor market indicators.	92	9
201403	404	2014-03-04	confcall	WEINBERG	Finally, we’re against including a reference to financial-stability concerns or financial market developments.	92	9
201403	405	2014-03-04	confcall	WEINBERG	Aside from a concern for financial stability, it’s not clear on what basis one would want to single out for special consideration the implication of financial market developments for our goals, compared with the full array of factors taken into consideration.	92	9
201403	406	2014-03-04	confcall	WEINBERG	Further, the notion of highlighting concerns about financial stability in a monetary policy context creates some difficulties.	92	9
201403	407	2014-03-04	confcall	WEINBERG	Would people conclude that the Committee would compromise on employment and inflation objectives for the sake of financial stability?	92	9
201403	408	2014-03-04	confcall	WEINBERG	Or would they conclude that large asset price increases would induce tighter monetary policy, or that large asset price declines would induce easier policy?	92	9
201403	409	2014-03-04	confcall	WEINBERG	Might they conclude that the Committee would ease policy in response to distress at one or more large financial institutions?	92	9
201403	410	2014-03-04	confcall	WEINBERG	Without a shared understanding of how financial market developments ought to enter into the monetary policy reaction function, communicating to the public about the role of financial-stability considerations could create more problems than it solves.	92	9
201403	411	2014-03-04	confcall	WEINBERG	Here again, further deliberations by the Committee on the relevant conceptual framework could be fruitful before expanding the dimensions of Committee communications further.	92	9
201403	412	2014-03-04	confcall	WEINBERG	Thank you.	92	9

201403	419	2014-03-04	confcall	PIANALTO	As today’s discussion demonstrates, the communication challenges before us are significant.	92	9
201403	420	2014-03-04	confcall	PIANALTO	In my view, we face two broad challenges.	92	9
201403	421	2014-03-04	confcall	PIANALTO	The first, and more pressing, challenge is communicating the conditions that will most likely lead to liftoff for the federal funds rate.	92	9
201403	422	2014-03-04	confcall	PIANALTO	The second is communicating the likely pace of adjustment after liftoff.	92	9
201403	423	2014-03-04	confcall	PIANALTO	The first challenge is simpler to address than the second, although I’m not sure, after today’s conversation, that it’s going to be quite that simple.	92	9
201403	424	2014-03-04	confcall	PIANALTO	But I do believe that our experiences, first with the date-based guidance and then with the unemployment thresholds for the fed funds rate liftoff, highlight the importance of proceeding cautiously with very broad changes to our forward guidance.	92	9
201403	425	2014-03-04	confcall	PIANALTO	For now, I suggest that the Committee focus on addressing the first challenge—that is, the timing of liftoff—and then take some time over the spring and summer to study and discuss the efficacy of approaches to guidance on the pace of adjustment after liftoff.	92	9
201403	426	2014-03-04	confcall	PIANALTO	To address the communications challenges around liftoff, in my view, it would be most effective to revise the forward guidance to simply refer to labor market conditions in broad terms and to establish an explicit inflation floor.	92	9
201403	427	2014-03-04	confcall	PIANALTO	In my economic outlook, the labor market will continue to improve gradually, and the inflation forecast is likely to be the key driver in the timing of liftoff.	92	9
201403	428	2014-03-04	confcall	PIANALTO	In addition, since the current statement language has an inflation ceiling and other wording that comes close to an inflation floor, the formal establishment of an inflation floor wouldn’t represent a large change in guidance or a large change in our approach.	92	9
201403	429	2014-03-04	confcall	PIANALTO	Of the forward-guidance options circulated to the Committee, I view option 5 as the best starting point because it provides continuity with the current statement and includes the full range of factors that the Committee will consider in deciding on liftoff.	92	9
201403	430	2014-03-04	confcall	PIANALTO	However, I believe that the reference in option 5 to “at least as long as complete recovery in the labor market appears to be more than a year away” could prove to be problematic.	92	9
201403	431	2014-03-04	confcall	PIANALTO	One reason that it could be problematic is that the Committee is likely to have difficulty in clearly defining a complete recovery in labor markets, just as we had some trouble with the guidance around the LSAP program that referred to a simpler notion of substantial improvement in the outlook for the labor market.	92	9
201403	432	2014-03-04	confcall	PIANALTO	A second reason that it might be problematic is that such guidance would imply that the Committee can accurately predict complete recovery in the labor market at least one year in advance, even though the simpler exercise of forecasting the unemployment rate over the last two years has been difficult.	92	9
201403	433	2014-03-04	confcall	PIANALTO	And a third reason is that we haven’t had the time for careful study of the efficacy of waiting to raise rates until just one year before the labor market recovery is complete.	92	9
201403	434	2014-03-04	confcall	PIANALTO	For these reasons, I would prefer a version of option 5 modified to drop the reference to complete recovery in labor markets, and, in place of that language, I would insert the inflation floor language that’s provided in the second sentence of option 3.	92	9
201403	435	2014-03-04	confcall	PIANALTO	The inflation forecast will capture many of the factors that are likely to determine liftoff, but they are more difficult to spell out in simple terms in the forward guidance.	92	9
201403	436	2014-03-04	confcall	PIANALTO	When you look at the December SEP, it suggests that using a 2 percent inflation floor would also be generally consistent with the Committee participants’ forecasts and policy views.	92	9
201403	437	2014-03-04	confcall	PIANALTO	Based on the limited information available in the December SEP, it looks as though the liftoff for many participants was being driven more by an inflation forecast than by the unemployment threshold.	92	9
201403	438	2014-03-04	confcall	PIANALTO	So, with those general comments, let me very quickly turn to the questions that were posed to the Committee.	92	9
201403	439	2014-03-04	confcall	PIANALTO	Regarding whether to include a general statement on policy decisions, I believe that it would be helpful to include the guidance that is provided in the second and the last sentences of option 5.	92	9
201403	440	2014-03-04	confcall	PIANALTO	I think any further general statement that the Committee wishes to make would best be presented in the annual Statement on Longer-Run Goals and Monetary Policy Strategy.	92	9
201403	441	2014-03-04	confcall	PIANALTO	As for linking liftoff to LSAPs, I believe that the statement language should preserve the guidance that’s provided in the current statement.	92	9
201403	442	2014-03-04	confcall	PIANALTO	To do otherwise might suggest a shift in our policy position.	92	9
201403	443	2014-03-04	confcall	PIANALTO	Regarding thresholds, triggers, and floors, as I just stated, I would prefer forward guidance that includes an inflation floor.	92	9
201403	444	2014-03-04	confcall	PIANALTO	In response to the second question, I believe that it is best to include financial developments or financial stability in the broader list of indicators that the Committee will be monitoring to decide on liftoff.	92	9
201403	445	2014-03-04	confcall	PIANALTO	And, in my view, the wording in option 5 is appropriate.	92	9
201403	446	2014-03-04	confcall	PIANALTO	In response to the third question, at this point, with liftoff likely to be some way off, market expectations seem to reflect an anticipation of gradual changes in the fed funds rate target after liftoff.	92	9
201403	447	2014-03-04	confcall	PIANALTO	So, at least for now, I don’t believe it’s necessary to add more-explicit language that could, over time, prove to require changes.	92	9
201403	448	2014-03-04	confcall	PIANALTO	Instead, as I’ve indicated, I’d prefer to focus now on addressing the challenges of liftoff communications and to use an inflation floor to address that issue.	92	9

201403	454	2014-03-04	confcall	GEORGE	Thank you, Madam Chair.	92	9
201403	455	2014-03-04	confcall	GEORGE	Like others, I’ve appreciated the opportunity to discuss the Committee’s forward guidance ahead of our March 18 meeting, and I, too, thank the staff for teeing up the options that we’re discussing today.	92	9
201403	456	2014-03-04	confcall	GEORGE	This exercise highlights, I think, the significant communications challenge that we face in the transition from unconventional aspects of our policy.	92	9
201403	457	2014-03-04	confcall	GEORGE	So, as I thought about the various options and the related implications and consequences, I gravitated to minimal changes at this point, continuing to simplify and clarify where possible rather than introducing new benchmarks or thresholds to describe the Committee’s sense of the future path of short-term rates.	92	9
201403	458	2014-03-04	confcall	GEORGE	To that end, I would support language along the lines of option 5 for our March statement, including the alternative drafted by President Plosser and sent out earlier, while leaning on other communications vehicles to elaborate.	92	9
201403	459	2014-03-04	confcall	GEORGE	And I want to also join in with those who have expressed concern within option 5 about that language of “complete recovery.”	92	9
201403	460	2014-03-04	confcall	GEORGE	I think that will pose some challenges in explaining what we mean by that.	92	9
201403	461	2014-03-04	confcall	GEORGE	In terms of the first and third questions, I would offer two thoughts on forward guidance relative to our existing strategy statement and the SEP.	92	9
201403	462	2014-03-04	confcall	GEORGE	I continue to think the Statement on Longer-Run Goals and Monetary Policy Strategy provides a good depiction of the Committee’s approach to its policy decisions.	92	9
201403	463	2014-03-04	confcall	GEORGE	The statement is clear, I think, that we account for deviations of inflation from its long-run goal and deviations of employment from our assessment of its maximum level while considering risk to the financial system.	92	9
201403	464	2014-03-04	confcall	GEORGE	It also explains the balanced approach we intend to pursue when these objectives are not complementary and describes that we account for the balance of risk when setting policy.	92	9
201403	465	2014-03-04	confcall	GEORGE	So this statement is an important complement to forward guidance, and I would not muddy future FOMC statements with further attempts to explain our approach to monetary strategy, since it’s likely to be either redundant or confusing.	92	9
201403	466	2014-03-04	confcall	GEORGE	In addition to leaning on our existing strategy statement, we should not underweight the value of the SEP in providing guidance on the path of rates after liftoff.	92	9
201403	467	2014-03-04	confcall	GEORGE	The SEP, despite its noted shortcomings, offers an ongoing and consistent framework that currently communicates the intention of Committee participants to keep the funds rate at an unusually low level to support the economy.	92	9
201403	468	2014-03-04	confcall	GEORGE	Unlike static dates or thresholds or other quantifications, which can move in unpredictable ways that don’t always align well with our policy intentions, the rate projections in the SEP over time will move in response to economic developments, providing information on how policy will vary with economic conditions after liftoff.	92	9
201403	469	2014-03-04	confcall	GEORGE	For this reason, I continue to believe that we could leverage the existing communication provided by the SEP to convey our future intentions by moving median projections of the funds rate into the FOMC statement.	92	9
201403	470	2014-03-04	confcall	GEORGE	One issue, of course, that’s been raised is whether the median should reflect all participants or only voting members.	92	9
201403	471	2014-03-04	confcall	GEORGE	And because the submissions today are not identified, I’m not sure whether this is an issue just in theory or in reality.	92	9
201403	472	2014-03-04	confcall	GEORGE	But a reference by the FOMC to the SEP would not be without precedent.	92	9
201403	473	2014-03-04	confcall	GEORGE	SEP medians are referenced today in our Statement on Longer-Run Goals and Monetary Policy Strategy, and they’re visibly attached to and described as part of the FOMC minutes at each submission.	92	9
201403	474	2014-03-04	confcall	GEORGE	Of course, in addition to these two vehicles, the press conferences and FOMC minutes can assist importantly with the heavy lifting of communicating our policy intentions.	92	9
201403	475	2014-03-04	confcall	GEORGE	In terms of question 2, on a more prominent role for financial developments, I tend to think that our Statement on Longer-Run Goals and Monetary Policy Strategy already references this.	92	9
201403	476	2014-03-04	confcall	GEORGE	But I could support including a sentence along the lines of that offered in option 4.	92	9
201403	477	2014-03-04	confcall	GEORGE	And, finally, I’ll conclude by saying that, in the longer term, I look forward to moving in the direction of statements like those that the staff shared from the Bank of England, whereby we can shift from some of our lengthy, complex statements to something more succinct and straightforward as we communicate our policy.	92	9
