201403	2566	2014-03-19	meeting	YELLEN	President Bullard.	23	2
201403	2567	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201403	2568	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	Basically, I think we’re in good shape for today.	23	2
201403	2569	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	We’re changing the form but not the substance of our forward guidance.	23	2
201403	2570	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	This is an appropriate time to be introducing such a change.	23	2
201403	2571	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	It’s widely anticipated in financial markets and elsewhere because we’re approaching the 6½ percent threshold.	23	2
201403	2572	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	This is making that kind of a number largely irrelevant for monetary policy considerations for the future.	23	2
201403	2573	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	Any change, I think, that we make carries potential risk in terms of market reaction, but, on the other hand, any market reaction will likely wash out after a few days because the fundamental policy is not really being altered at this meeting.	23	2
201403	2574	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	So I support alternative B for today.	23	2
201403	2575	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	I have two remarks on alternative B and then some reactions to some of the previous comments ahead of me here today.	23	2
201403	2576	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	The first comment is on the wisdom of paragraph 7, and the second comment is on the wisdom of putting too much time dependence into the statement and into the Committee’s thinking.	23	2
201403	2577	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	Concerning paragraph 7, this paragraph is meant to reassure markets that nothing has changed in terms of the level of policy accommodation.	23	2
201403	2578	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	In general, I think it’s not good practice to include paragraphs in the statement that purport to explain the meaning of changes elsewhere in the statement.	23	2
201403	2579	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	In effect, we’re footnoting the statement.	23	2
201403	2580	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	One could imagine footnoting other parts of the statement that contain changes.	23	2
201403	2581	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	You could footnote the strength of housing, which is changed in paragraph 1, for example, and you might cite some of the more recent data on housing and indicate why we changed that part of the statement—because the data are a little bit different from what they were.	23	2
201403	2582	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	We might also say in that footnote that this doesn’t necessarily mean that the Committee had changed its policy because we changed slightly our view of the most recent housing data.	23	2
201403	2583	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	This kind of tactic strikes me as self-referential, and it seems circular and somewhat counterproductive to me.	23	2
201403	2584	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	Having said all of that, I understand what we’re trying to do here, and I may be persuaded that, just for today, given the somewhat special circumstances—it being the Chair’s first meeting and press conference—it may strengthen our hand.	23	2
201403	2585	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	But I think the more appropriate approach would be just to omit paragraph 7 and use the press conference to communicate more fully the meaning of the statement.	23	2
201403	2586	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	That’s how this is set up, and, for other changes in the statement, we wouldn’t include a special provision at the end to say something about the meaning of it.	23	2
201403	2587	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	All right.	23	2
201403	2588	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	Let me turn to time dependence.	23	2
201403	2589	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	I’m going to refer here to the “considerable time” phrase in paragraph 5 of alternative B, which is meant to convey a waiting period between the end of the asset purchase program and the date of liftoff.	23	2
201403	2590	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	I understand that, in principle, this is a state-contingent object, but I do not think that it conveys sufficient state dependence as written.	23	2
201403	2591	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	For most market participants and maybe most FOMC participants around this table, it means a fixed amount of time without too much regard for what happens in the economy.	23	2
201403	2592	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	In many cases, as President Lockhart noted, it might mean six months.	23	2
201403	2593	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	I do not think we can change this today, but I do think the Committee should continually strive to express itself in state-contingent terms.	23	2
201403	2594	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	One of the main dangers of calendar-based thinking is that, when the calendar says that it is time to make a move, the economy may be saying something else, and this Committee has, in several circumstances, run into exactly that kind of problem.	23	2
201403	2595	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	We had a calendar date circled in our minds.	23	2
201403	2596	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	We got to that date, and the circumstances weren’t right.	23	2
201403	2597	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	And that creates a mismatch between what policy should be doing and what it’s actually doing.	23	2
201403	2598	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	The SEP contributes to this problem, especially with the date of liftoff in 2014, 2015, and 2016, a date that receives a laser-like focus in financial markets.	23	2
201403	2599	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	I agree completely with Vice Chairman Dudley’s comments yesterday that this needs a revamp.	23	2
201403	2600	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	We have looked at it before.	23	2
201403	2601	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	It’s a difficult issue.	23	2
201403	2602	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	I understand that.	23	2
201403	2603	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	I do think that there may be a very simple change that we could make in the near term.	23	2
201403	2604	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	As we’re getting closer to the date of liftoff, it might pay to make the SEP more granular with respect to the date of liftoff.	23	2
201403	2605	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	You could have a special question in the SEP that would ask not just “What year are you anticipating liftoff?” but also “What quarter are you anticipating the date of liftoff?”	23	2
201403	2606	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	And you could plot that separately.	23	2
201403	2607	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	It makes a big difference.	23	2
201403	2608	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	I was the one who changed from 2014 to 2015, but it was really 2014, fourth quarter, to 2015, first quarter.	23	2
201403	2609	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	So I moved over a bin in the picture, and, the way this gets reported, somebody will say something about that.	23	2
201403	2610	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	But it might be more informative as we get closer if we start talking about the quarter of liftoff currently expected based on the data.	23	2
201403	2611	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	That would be a very simple change.	23	2
201403	2612	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	It might convey a little bit more.	23	2
201403	2613	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	Longer term, I do think we need a more substantial revamp of the SEP.	23	2
201403	2614	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	I would urge all of you to consider a renewed attempt at a monetary policy report.	23	2
201403	2615	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	I know we tried to do that earlier.	23	2
201403	2616	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	It didn’t work out, but I think that maybe the perspective has changed.	23	2
201403	2617	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	We’re a little bit closer to normal policy now, and it might be the time to, again, renew that issue.	23	2
201403	2618	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	I know we had thoughts about that at previous meetings, and we probably have plans on the table, but, eventually, I think the future of this Committee is that we’re going to have to have a monetary policy report that summarizes, in some way, the view of the Committee so that markets can absorb what we’re thinking as a group.	23	2
201403	2619	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	Concerning the 2016 SEP policy rate, which has moved up somewhat, I guess I’m convinced that what we should do on that is just cite lower unemployment.	23	2
201403	2620	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	Unemployment has moved down considerably from where it was at the time of the December meeting.	23	2
201403	2621	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	So, logically, that’s going to cause a few people to adjust slightly the setting they think we’re going to have for the policy rate in 2016.	23	2
201403	2622	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	I think that’s the simplest and cleanest thing to say.	23	2
201403	2623	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	We don’t have to talk about changing membership or other things like that.	23	2
201403	2624	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	It’s true that the growth forecast is actually going in the wrong direction.	23	2
201403	2625	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	So I would just cite labor markets and say that that looks better than it did, and that it probably caused some people to move up slightly.	23	2
201403	2626	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	I’m going to react to a few things people have said.	23	2
201403	2627	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	In paragraph 6, the second sentence—“keeping ... rates below”—I agree with President Plosser that the story behind this is not clear.	23	2
201403	2628	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	As I have described it here before, there are, in my mind, three explanations for the low policy rate in 2016, which, again, is occurring after output gaps have closed and after inflation has returned to target.	23	2
201403	2629	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	These three explanations, which were touched on by Governor Tarullo here, are as follows:  First, there’s the headwinds explanation, which, in my mind, means that there are some unspecified shocks that are going to hit the economy at this distant date in the future.	23	2
201403	2630	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	I think that’s a difficult story to tell.	23	2
201403	2631	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	How could we, sitting here today, know what these shocks are going to be?	23	2
201403	2632	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	I also think it sends a pessimistic signal about our view of the future of the US economy, and it’s an unwarranted pessimistic signal.	23	2
201403	2633	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	We don’t really know what the world is going to be like in 2016.	23	2
201403	2634	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	So the headwinds explanation is one possible explanation.	23	2
201403	2635	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	The second is the Woodford explanation, which I see has become less and less popular here.	23	2
201403	2636	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	The Woodford explanation would be that we’re keeping rates low at that point because we’re making up for the time when we were constrained by the zero bound.	23	2
201403	2637	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	The Woodford story, even though it’s become less popular here, has a great aspect to it, which is that it’s an optimistic story.	23	2
201403	2638	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	You say that, yes, the economy will be booming at that time and we’re still keeping rates low, but there’s a good reason why we’re doing that.	23	2
201403	2639	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	It’s because we’re following through on our commitment that we made earlier.	23	2
201403	2640	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	I know that that one is not being used, and it’s not that popular.	23	2
201403	2641	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	The third one is that real interest rates are lower and will continue to be lower in 2016 than they have been historically.	23	2
201403	2642	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	I would put a global aspect on that.	23	2
201403	2643	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	Global real interest rates are lower than they have been historically, and that’s why, when you add the real interest rate to the inflation target, you get a somewhat lower neutral policy rate than you would have when you looked at the 1980s, the 1990s, or the 2000s.	23	2
201403	2644	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	Among the three explanations, this one has, I think, the most potential for the Committee to rally around.	23	2
201403	2645	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	It has a pessimistic tinge to it if you think that the real rates are lower because of lower potential growth for the US economy.	23	2
201403	2646	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	If you told it as a global story, which I think is very plausible—as a global saving glut, let’s say, which is keeping real interest rates low—then it would not necessarily have to have a pessimistic signal from the US point of view.	23	2
201403	2647	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	It certainly seems to be true that global real interest rates have been uncharacteristically low for quite a while, that that would persist out into the future, and that that might be an important factor as to why the neutral policy rate won’t be as high as it has been historically.	23	2
201403	2648	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	My own SEP has us back at a 4 percent or 4¼ percent policy rate by that time period because I have output gaps closed, I have inflation back at target, I’m not expecting any special shocks at that time, and I’m not putting that much weight on this story of low global real interest rates persisting that far out into the future.	23	2
201403	2649	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	We’re often using the headwinds explanation in public comments, but I do not think it’s very effective, and that’s why we keep getting a lot of questions about it.	23	2
201403	2650	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	It just raises a lot of questions in the minds of market participants.	23	2
201403	2651	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	Somehow shocks are going to be hitting the economy at that time, or shocks that are still around today are superpersistent, and yet persistent in a way that’s not preventing the output gap from closing and inflation from going back to target.	23	2
201403	2652	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	This is a very difficult way to go about telling a story.	23	2
201403	2653	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	Why have these shocks not affected the output or inflation gaps?	23	2
201403	2654	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	So I think that the explanation of low global real interest rates is somewhat more effective, and that we should switch to this explanation in the future.	23	2
201403	2655	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	My last comment concerns mentioning “keeping short-term interest rates below”	23	2
201403	2656	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	—I guess there’s a lot of agreement on this.	23	2
201403	2657	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	I’d be for replacing that with “keeping the federal funds rate below levels the Committee views as normal” in paragraph 6, as noted earlier by President Plosser.	23	2
201403	2658	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	So I favor that particular change.	23	2
201403	2659	2014-03-19	meeting	BULLARD	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2

201403	2661	2014-03-19	meeting	YELLEN	President George.	23	2
201403	2662	2014-03-19	meeting	GEORGE	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201403	2663	2014-03-19	meeting	GEORGE	I generally support alternative B in terms of a further reduction in asset purchases and a pivot from threshold-based forward guidance to a more qualitative approach.	23	2
201403	2664	2014-03-19	meeting	GEORGE	I view these changes as appropriate steps toward gradual policy normalization as the economy continues to expand, with meaningful cumulative gains as well as a positive growth outlook.	23	2
201403	2665	2014-03-19	meeting	GEORGE	As someone noted yesterday, most of the prescriptions from the policy rules on which the Committee has relied over the past five years also have turned positive, in terms of signaling a shift away from zero interest rates starting in the second quarter of this year.	23	2
201403	2666	2014-03-19	meeting	GEORGE	For these reasons, I think paragraph 6, as written, lacks clarity as to why economic conditions warrant keeping rates below normal levels when employment and inflation begin to return to normal.	23	2
201403	2667	2014-03-19	meeting	GEORGE	Further explanation of the Committee’s assumptions about economic conditions in 2016 will be needed, in my view, to be credible.	23	2
201403	2668	2014-03-19	meeting	GEORGE	At last September’s press conference, factors such as continued fiscal drag and the slow recovery of the housing sector were offered as explanations.	23	2
201403	2669	2014-03-19	meeting	GEORGE	The January 2014 minutes point to lingering effects of the crisis.	23	2
201403	2670	2014-03-19	meeting	GEORGE	However, the Tealbook now shows almost no fiscal drag in 2016, with substantial gains in residential construction.	23	2
201403	2671	2014-03-19	meeting	GEORGE	So as the Committee alters its forward guidance, I expect that the public will seek more clarity about the nature of our reaction function, and I look forward to discussing that communication.	23	2
201403	2672	2014-03-19	meeting	GEORGE	That said, I would highlight a few issues that continue to concern me about this policy stance.	23	2
201403	2673	2014-03-19	meeting	GEORGE	First, in thinking about the potential challenges that may lie ahead, I believe that the alternative risk scenarios outlined in the Tealbook are useful.	23	2
201403	2674	2014-03-19	meeting	GEORGE	In particular, I see the “Supply- Side Damage” scenario as one of the more relevant and difficult scenarios to navigate, primarily because it would necessitate policy tightening faster than currently anticipated.	23	2
201403	2675	2014-03-19	meeting	GEORGE	Growth would also likely disappoint in such a scenario, so banks and other financial institutions would be grappling simultaneously with rates that are climbing faster than they had expected and slowing growth.	23	2
201403	2676	2014-03-19	meeting	GEORGE	Aspects of this scenario seem plausible, especially given the downward revisions to potential GDP by the Congressional Budget Office and in the Tealbook.	23	2
201403	2677	2014-03-19	meeting	GEORGE	Second, I remain concerned about the side effects of unusually low interest rates for this extended period of time and the incentives they promote for risk-taking and reaching for yield.	23	2
201403	2678	2014-03-19	meeting	GEORGE	I continue to hear from contacts about fierce competition among lenders resulting in questionable terms and underwriting standards.	23	2
201403	2679	2014-03-19	meeting	GEORGE	And I would note that consumer credit growth is beginning to accelerate, up nearly $300 billion in the second half of 2013, which does not include student loans.	23	2
201403	2680	2014-03-19	meeting	GEORGE	Some of this goes hand in hand with an improving housing market.	23	2
201403	2681	2014-03-19	meeting	GEORGE	If you look carefully at the data, it is the least creditworthy households that are more actively increasing their debt burdens.	23	2
201403	2682	2014-03-19	meeting	GEORGE	Finally, I would join others who would prefer that paragraph 6 refer to the target federal funds rate instead of short-term interest rates so that we can continue our discussions about what the policy framework might look like in the future.	23	2
201403	2683	2014-03-19	meeting	GEORGE	Thank you.	23	2
201403	2684	2014-03-19	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	23	2

201403	2727	2014-03-19	meeting	YELLEN	President Kocherlakota.	23	2
201403	2728	2014-03-19	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201403	2729	2014-03-19	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I see today’s FOMC statement as a significant one.	23	2
201403	2730	2014-03-19	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Over the past few months, we’ve had a fulsome discussion about the best way to communicate about the evolution of the fed funds rate target once the unemployment rate falls below 6.5 percent.	23	2
201403	2731	2014-03-19	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Thanks in part to your leadership, Madam Chair, this has been a thoughtful and deliberative process, which is culminating today in alternative B.	23	2
201403	2732	2014-03-19	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	But I have decided to vote against alternative B.	23	2
201403	2733	2014-03-19	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I am dissenting because the new forward guidance weakens the credibility of the commitment to return inflation to the 2 percent target from below, and because it fosters policy uncertainty that hinders economic activity.	23	2
201403	2734	2014-03-19	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I do strongly endorse the language in paragraph 6, with the emendation that President Plosser offered.	23	2
201403	2735	2014-03-19	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	But my enthusiasm for that paragraph is not sufficient to change my vote.	23	2
201403	2736	2014-03-19	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I’ll briefly elaborate on my dissent.	23	2
201403	2737	2014-03-19	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	In terms of credibility, the PCE inflation rate has tended downward over the past few years and is currently near 1 percent.	23	2
201403	2738	2014-03-19	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Tealbook A does not see the inflation rate returning to 2 percent until 2018.	23	2
201403	2739	2014-03-19	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	This is six years after we publicly committed to 2 percent as our target.	23	2
201403	2740	2014-03-19	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The FOMC should communicate the purposeful steps that are being taken to facilitate a more rapid return of inflation to target.	23	2
201403	2741	2014-03-19	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The absence of this kind of communication weakens the credibility of the Committee’s inflation target by suggesting that the Committee views inflation persistently below 2 percent as an acceptable outcome.	23	2
201403	2742	2014-03-19	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	In terms of uncertainty, most labor market metrics imply that the economy is still well short of maximum employment.	23	2
201403	2743	2014-03-19	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	In its forward guidance in alternative B, the Committee provides little information about its desired rate of progress toward maximum employment.	23	2
201403	2744	2014-03-19	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Indeed, the guidance provides no quantitative measure of what constitutes maximum employment.	23	2
201403	2745	2014-03-19	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	These omissions foster uncertainty about the extent to which the Committee is willing to use monetary stimulus to foster faster growth, and this uncertainty acts as a drag on economic activity.	23	2
201403	2746	2014-03-19	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	What could we have done instead?	23	2
201403	2747	2014-03-19	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	In my view, over the past 15 months, the Committee’s forward guidance about the fed funds rate has been highly effective at managing market expectations.	23	2
201403	2748	2014-03-19	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	That guidance has relied on an unemployment rate threshold of 6.5 percent and an inflation outlook guardrail of 2½ percent.	23	2
201403	2749	2014-03-19	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Because of the effectiveness of this quantitative approach, I would have favored adopting a similar approach for the future.	23	2
201403	2750	2014-03-19	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	To be even more specific, my preferred language would have been as follows: “The Committee anticipates keeping the fed funds rate in its current range at least until the unemployment rate has fallen below 5.5 percent, as long as the one- to two-year-ahead outlook for PCE inflation remains below 2¼ percent, longer-term inflation expectations remain well anchored, and possible risks to financial stability remain well contained.”	23	2
201403	2751	2014-03-19	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	This alternative guidance communicates a willingness to use monetary policy to push inflation back up to 2 percent.	23	2
201403	2752	2014-03-19	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	It reduces macroeconomic uncertainty by being clear about the kinds of labor market and inflation conditions that are likely to be associated with an increase in the federal funds rate.	23	2
201403	2753	2014-03-19	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Finally, it deals with what I see as the unlikely possibility of risks to financial stability through an explicit escape clause.	23	2
201403	2754	2014-03-19	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Here, I’m going a little bit off my script.	23	2
201403	2755	2014-03-19	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	A question that occurs to people, I think, is, will we always need quantitative forward guidance?	23	2
201403	2756	2014-03-19	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Aren’t we back to normal now, so can’t we just get rid of this extraordinary tool that we used during extraordinary times?	23	2
201403	2757	2014-03-19	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	And here, I think, the problem for us is that we can’t go back to normal—as, say, we were doing in 2004 or 2006— because of the fact that we’ve made a change in what our framework is.	23	2
201403	2758	2014-03-19	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	We now have an explicit number that operates as our target—2 percent.	23	2
201403	2759	2014-03-19	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	That means we have to communicate numerically about how we’re doing in terms of making progress toward that goal.	23	2
201403	2760	2014-03-19	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	If we had a monetary policy report that was communicating on a consistent basis about what the Committee’s outlook was, depending on its policy, and that described the Committee’s plans on an ongoing basis for how it was planning to ameliorate any gaps between its current outcomes and the target on both the employment and inflation dimensions, we wouldn’t have to have all of this in the statement.	23	2
201403	2761	2014-03-19	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	It would be, instead, in the monetary policy report.	23	2
201403	2762	2014-03-19	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Here I’m fully aware that President Bullard probably disagrees with what I would have in the report, but I think having that kind of communication would eliminate the need to have this in the statement.	23	2
201403	2763	2014-03-19	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	We’re not at that stage.	23	2
201403	2764	2014-03-19	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I’ll close by noting again that I do strongly endorse paragraph 6, with the particular emendation of replacing “short-term interest rates” with “the target for the federal funds rate.”	23	2
201403	2765	2014-03-19	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think this paragraph provides information about the Committee’s intentions for the behavior of the fed funds rate once employment and inflation are near mandate-consistent levels.	23	2
201403	2766	2014-03-19	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	From an intellectual point of view, I’m sure it’s very interesting to try to figure out why we’re doing this.	23	2
201403	2767	2014-03-19	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	That’s not something we usually insist on—having agreement among the Committee about why we’re doing things.	23	2
201403	2768	2014-03-19	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	And these meetings will get very long indeed if we try to insist on that.	23	2
201403	2769	2014-03-19	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think this is providing the public with the information they need about the covariance structure of the mandate variables and our policy tool:  Employment and inflation are going to be near mandate-consistent levels, and the fed funds rate is going to remain below historical norms.	23	2
201403	2770	2014-03-19	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Those intentions are appropriate, and communicating them should help stimulate economic activity by reducing uncertainty.	23	2
201403	2771	2014-03-19	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201403	2772	2014-03-19	meeting	YELLEN	Thank you.	23	2

201403	2792	2014-03-19	meeting	STEIN	Another dimension is, where does the guidance fall on a spectrum, with one end of the spectrum being “Commitment” and the other end being “Well, this is kind of my forecast, but don’t take it too seriously”?	23	2

201403	2828	2014-03-19	meeting	POWELL	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201403	2829	2014-03-19	meeting	POWELL	I will support alternative B, and I’ll come to the statement language in the end.	23	2
201403	2830	2014-03-19	meeting	POWELL	As Stan Fischer suggested five days ago in our confirmation hearing, the process of returning monetary policy to a normal stance has now begun.	23	2
201403	2831	2014-03-19	meeting	POWELL	Along the way, I expressed a fair amount of concern that the Committee could lose control of the current asset purchase program because of what I saw as the lack of a stopping rule that covered most of the reasonably likely outcomes, and I’m very pleased to note that that didn’t happen.	23	2
201403	2832	2014-03-19	meeting	POWELL	Instead, the Committee is going to reduce purchases today for the third consecutive meeting.	23	2
201403	2833	2014-03-19	meeting	POWELL	On net, the market has barely reacted, and market participants seem comfortable with the path.	23	2
201403	2834	2014-03-19	meeting	POWELL	This is a big win, and it’s a very good start for the normalization process.	23	2
201403	2835	2014-03-19	meeting	POWELL	But, having been cautious about getting this far in, I’m going to suggest the need for caution on the way out because the process of normalization is itself an important threat to the recovery, and there’s a need to steer a middle course between possible bad outcomes.	23	2
201403	2836	2014-03-19	meeting	POWELL	Lots of risks are outside our control, but, to control the arguably controllable, I want to talk about two risks in particular.	23	2
201403	2837	2014-03-19	meeting	POWELL	The first is that, for one of two reasons, the market suddenly pulls forward liftoff and drives up rates across the curve in a way that threatens the economy.	23	2
201403	2838	2014-03-19	meeting	POWELL	We’ve already seen the large effect on housing from a pretty modest increase in mortgage rates.	23	2
201403	2839	2014-03-19	meeting	POWELL	Housing finance is still historically cheap, but, nonetheless, we’ve seen the housing recovery really affected by it.	23	2
201403	2840	2014-03-19	meeting	POWELL	I think it’s important to keep in mind that this is still a fragile recovery, which can be threatened in this way.	23	2
201403	2841	2014-03-19	meeting	POWELL	Now, the market, of course, is supposed to react to good and bad economic news, and, if that’s the source of the surprise and the source of the reaction, then it’s one that the Committee can and must manage.	23	2
201403	2842	2014-03-19	meeting	POWELL	I think the way to protect against it is to tie down forward guidance, and that’s one of the reasons I support the last sentence in paragraph 6.	23	2
201403	2843	2014-03-19	meeting	POWELL	I’ll come to some others later.	23	2
201403	2844	2014-03-19	meeting	POWELL	But, to me, the idea is to build a framework that will be resilient to the kind of events in which the economy strengthens, and so in the period ahead I’d like to see us tie down guidance.	23	2
201403	2845	2014-03-19	meeting	POWELL	It’s not going to be perfect, as I’ll get to.	23	2
201403	2846	2014-03-19	meeting	POWELL	On the other hand, we need to be very careful not to send a signal that our reaction function has changed.	23	2
201403	2847	2014-03-19	meeting	POWELL	A tightening that’s not based on stronger economic news could stop and reverse progress.	23	2
201403	2848	2014-03-19	meeting	POWELL	We could find ourselves having to gear up asset purchases again, and that is not a place that I aspire to be.	23	2
201403	2849	2014-03-19	meeting	POWELL	The second risk is that, even without a sudden reevaluation of the policy, financial instability emerges in the form of unsustainably exuberant financial conditions and the risk of a sudden reversal that stops the economy in its tracks.	23	2
201403	2850	2014-03-19	meeting	POWELL	I think it’s a very real threat, though perhaps not in the very near term.	23	2
201403	2851	2014-03-19	meeting	POWELL	And, unfortunately, it’s one that the Committee is not very well equipped to handle except through monetary policy, a famously blunt instrument.	23	2
201403	2852	2014-03-19	meeting	POWELL	Just a word on today’s conditions.	23	2
201403	2853	2014-03-19	meeting	POWELL	I would call them mixed but trending toward ebullience.	23	2
201403	2854	2014-03-19	meeting	POWELL	On the equity markets, I really think that the level of the equity markets is a function of the debate over the sustainability of profit margins at very high levels, and that’s what drives things like valuation-to-GDP, Tobin’s q, cyclically adjusted P/E, and valuation-to-sales.	23	2
201403	2855	2014-03-19	meeting	POWELL	As yesterday’s staff presentation showed, P/Es are not unsustainably high.	23	2
201403	2856	2014-03-19	meeting	POWELL	On the question of whether profit margins are at an unsustainable level, I not only don’t know, but also don’t know how to know.	23	2
201403	2857	2014-03-19	meeting	POWELL	I think we’ll just have to stick around and find out.	23	2
201403	2858	2014-03-19	meeting	POWELL	As far as leveraged finance markets are concerned, I thought Jeremy covered it well yesterday.	23	2
201403	2859	2014-03-19	meeting	POWELL	We’re not at peak-level ebullience, but we’re in the same Zip code, and we have rates that are going to remain low for years ahead.	23	2
201403	2860	2014-03-19	meeting	POWELL	So it’s plausible to me that our policy could push the price of financial assets much higher and set up a reaction that could significantly harm the economy.	23	2
201403	2861	2014-03-19	meeting	POWELL	It’s not a prediction, but I think it’s a real risk.	23	2
201403	2862	2014-03-19	meeting	POWELL	And the policy implications of that are difficult as well.	23	2
201403	2863	2014-03-19	meeting	POWELL	Let me say what I think success would look like.	23	2
201403	2864	2014-03-19	meeting	POWELL	A successful middle course between those two risks will obviously involve rates moving up and volatility returning to normal levels as the economy improves.	23	2
201403	2865	2014-03-19	meeting	POWELL	The process is almost guaranteed to be bumpy and jagged and not smooth, and we need to accept and embrace the messiness.	23	2
201403	2866	2014-03-19	meeting	POWELL	In a way, the kinds of increases in volatility that come with a stronger economy should be welcomed.	23	2
201403	2867	2014-03-19	meeting	POWELL	If we have the right framework in place—and the markets always overshoot, except when you expect them to overshoot, so we need to embrace that if it happens and let the market get comfortable.	23	2
201403	2868	2014-03-19	meeting	POWELL	And we need to avoid self-inflicted wounds.	23	2
201403	2869	2014-03-19	meeting	POWELL	The third potential risk—that of an overheating economy, as I suggested yesterday— seems to me remote.	23	2
201403	2870	2014-03-19	meeting	POWELL	The economy may very well prove tighter than it appears and tighter than I think it is, but, given the pace at which it’s moving, it’s really hard to see the economy sneaking up on us on this.	23	2
201403	2871	2014-03-19	meeting	POWELL	It’s a risk that, if it emerges, can be addressed with the standard playbook.	23	2
201403	2872	2014-03-19	meeting	POWELL	In the meantime, the strategy should be as transparent and predictable as possible to move at a stately pace, and, yes, I’m happy to join Jeremy and Richard in tiptoeing through the tulips and off the field.	23	2

201403	2886	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	Thank you, Madam Chair.	23	2
201403	2887	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	Well, I support alternative B.	23	2
201403	2888	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	I think it’s important to revamp the statement before the unemployment rate reaches the 6½ percent threshold, for several reasons.	23	2
201403	2889	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	First of all, it allows us to preempt the question of what happens when the threshold is actually reached.	23	2
201403	2890	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	If we kept the threshold in today’s statement and then the unemployment rate declined, that would raise all sorts of questions about what would happen at the subsequent meeting, and we might not have the press conference scheduled as a vehicle to explain ourselves.	23	2
201403	2891	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	So, doing it preemptively, I think, makes a lot of sense because it just takes it off the table.	23	2
201403	2892	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	Second, I don’t think the 6½ percent unemployment rate threshold adds much value currently.	23	2
201403	2893	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	If you look at the SEP numbers or you look at the market expectations, everyone thinks that we’re going to wait long past the time when the unemployment rate gets below 6½ percent.	23	2
201403	2894	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	So it’s not as though there’s a lot of information content in that.	23	2
201403	2895	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	I recognize that removing it does create the question of whether that threshold still applies in terms of our behavior, but I think that’s taken care of by paragraph 7.	23	2
201403	2896	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	I also think it’s essential to add the language in both sentences of paragraph 6.	23	2
201403	2897	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	Financial conditions are determined in large part not just by the timing of liftoff, but also by the trajectory of short-term interest rates after that.	23	2
201403	2898	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	So if you omitted the second sentence in paragraph 6, you’re basically not telling people what you think is likely to happen after liftoff, and that’s a very important component of what drives financial conditions.	23	2
201403	2899	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	If you don’t provide that guidance, that implies greater uncertainty, greater volatility, and higher risk premiums, which go against what we’re trying to accomplish.	23	2
201403	2900	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	That said, I think it’s very important not to oversell paragraph 6, and my view here is very close to Governor Stein’s.	23	2
201403	2901	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	Our expectations may not be realized.	23	2
201403	2902	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	So there’s still plenty of residual uncertainty about the outlook.	23	2
201403	2903	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	We can’t eliminate the underlying uncertainty about the economic outlook and the path of short-term rates that’s consistent with that outlook, but we certainly can eliminate that portion of uncertainty about our own current thinking about what we’re expecting to do.	23	2
201403	2904	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	We should share our current thinking, recognizing that what we think and how this will translate into our actions will evolve over time.	23	2
201403	2905	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	There’s not much pre-commitment here at all, in my opinion.	23	2
201403	2906	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	I also think adding paragraph 6 today has the benefit of getting the post-liftoff forward guidance into the statement at an early enough stage that it’s not going to be taken as a signal of impending liftoff.	23	2
201403	2907	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	If we didn’t do it today, taking advantage of Chair Yellen’s first meeting as the head of the Committee and the fact that we’re close to 6½ percent on the unemployment rate, then we’d have these questions of when we would add it and how the market would take it as a signal at that time.	23	2
201403	2908	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	Looking at the statement, I think that, if we didn’t have the SEP problem, the markets could actually digest paragraph 6 quite easily, especially with paragraph 7 emphasizing that a revamp of the statement does not change the guidance.	23	2
201403	2909	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	The problem is not the statement.	23	2
201403	2910	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	The problem is the SEP dots in 2016.	23	2
201403	2911	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	What about the substance of paragraph 6—that the neutral level of interest rates is likely to be below the historical average for some time?	23	2
201403	2912	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	That can be justified in many ways.	23	2
201403	2913	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	First, if the equilibrium real rate were really close to the historical average of 2 percent, then I would think we’d be growing a lot more rapidly than we actually have been growing, given that the current real interest rate is minus 1 percent.	23	2
201403	2914	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	Second, on the headwinds side, it’s probably important for us to talk a little bit more about this.	23	2
201403	2915	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	What exactly are these headwinds?	23	2
201403	2916	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	I see two broad sets of headwinds.	23	2
201403	2917	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	On the investment side, I see lots of reasons why investment is weak— for example, homeowners who don’t have much equity in their houses or are even underwater on their mortgages, so they can’t get new mortgages, they can’t refinance, and they can’t move.	23	2
201403	2918	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	Also, in the mortgage market, you see sharp differentiation on the availability of mortgage credit based on FICO scores, which is very different than what’s applied historically.	23	2
201403	2919	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	I think there are still constraints on credit to small business start-ups.	23	2
201403	2920	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	So a whole bunch of things are constraining the investment side.	23	2
201403	2921	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	On the saving side, there are lots of reasons to think that the crisis has caused a shift in the saving function to greater precautionary saving.	23	2
201403	2922	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	When I started to think of it conceptually, I thought of it as, the IS curve has shifted to the left—you basically have less investment and more saving, and so that’s really pulling down the equilibrium real rate for a period of time.	23	2
201403	2923	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	It would be good for us to try to articulate that a little bit more fully.	23	2
201403	2924	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	The third thing I want to talk about a little bit is something that hasn’t been discussed.	23	2
201403	2925	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	I really do think the effect of monetary policy on economic activity depends on both the level of interest rates and the change in the level of interest rates, and I don’t think we’ve had any discussion about that.	23	2
201403	2926	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	We saw over the last year what the effects of the increase in mortgage rates were on the housing market—we saw a pretty significant slowing in the housing market.	23	2
201403	2927	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	I would encourage the staff to look at this question—that is, as interest rates rise, how much of a restraint will that change in financial conditions exert on the economy, even if we’re still at an accommodative monetary policy setting?	23	2
201403	2928	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	This is something that, when I worked in the private sector, we really struggled with.	23	2
201403	2929	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	Is it the level of financial conditions, or is it the change of financial conditions, that actually affects economic growth?	23	2
201403	2930	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	I’d like to see more work done on this so we could understand that a little bit.	23	2
201403	2931	2014-03-19	meeting	DUDLEY	It’s relevant now because we’re just so far away from the equilibrium real rate that we think is going to apply over the longer term.	23	2
